Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
The National Digital Resilience Agency (NDRA) is tasked with safeguarding critical digital infrastructure across the nation. Faced with evolving cyber threats and physical vulnerabilities, the NDRA must efficiently allocate its limited defense resources to protect various strategic digital assets, aiming to maximize the overall digital defense capability. The agency defines its defense capability based on the strategic importance of each location and the level of resources deployed there.

The NDRA has identified four key strategic digital infrastructure locations that require continuous protection:
1.  **National Data Center (NDC)**: A high-importance facility storing sensitive government and citizen data.
2.  **Primary Network Hub (PNH)**: A central node for national internet traffic and communication, vital for connectivity.
3.  **Cloud Infrastructure Gateway (CIG)**: The main access point for critical cloud services used by public and private sectors.
4.  **Regional Backup Data Center (RBDC)**: A secondary facility providing data redundancy and disaster recovery for regional digital services.

Each of these locations has been assigned a 'Defense Importance Score' reflecting its criticality to national security and operational continuity:
*   National Data Center (NDC): 10
*   Primary Network Hub (PNH): 8
*   Cloud Infrastructure Gateway (CIG): 7
*   Regional Backup Data Center (RBDC): 5

To fortify these locations, the NDRA has access to four types of specialized defense resources, which can be deployed in continuous units (e.g., fractional units representing partial assignments or shared access):
1.  **Cybersecurity Analysts (CSA)**: Highly skilled personnel specializing in threat detection, analysis, and rapid response.
2.  **Physical Security Personnel (PSP)**: Guards and surveillance experts ensuring the physical integrity and access control of facilities.
3.  **Advanced Threat Detection Systems (ATDS)**: Specialized software and hardware units providing real-time threat intelligence and anomaly detection.
4.  **Network Redundancy Modules (NRM)**: Hardware components designed to enhance network uptime, resilience, and resistance to denial-of-service attacks.

The total available units of each resource across the entire NDRA are limited as follows:
*   Cybersecurity Analysts (CSA): 30 units
*   Physical Security Personnel (PSP): 40 units
*   Advanced Threat Detection Systems (ATDS): 25 units
*   Network Redundancy Modules (NRM): 20 units

Deploying these resources incurs varying costs, which depend on the specific location due to logistical challenges, operational environments, and local compensation rates. The cost of deploying one unit of each resource type to each location (in thousands of dollars) is detailed below:

| Resource Type                 | National Data Center (NDC) | Primary Network Hub (PNH) | Cloud Infrastructure Gateway (CIG) | Regional Backup Data Center (RBDC) |
| :---------------------------- | :------------------------- | :------------------------ | :--------------------------------- | :--------------------------------- |
| Cybersecurity Analysts (CSA)  | 80                         | 75                        | 70                                 | 65                                 |
| Physical Security Personnel (PSP) | 50                         | 45                        | 40                                 | 35                                 |
| Advanced Threat Detection Systems (ATDS) | 60                         | 55                        | 50                                 | 45                                 |
| Network Redundancy Modules (NRM) | 40                         | 35                        | 30                                 | 25                                 |

Furthermore, each strategic location has an independently allocated operational budget that cannot be exceeded for its defense measures (in thousands of dollars):
*   National Data Center (NDC): 1,500
*   Primary Network Hub (PNH): 1,000
*   Cloud Infrastructure Gateway (CIG): 900
*   Regional Backup Data Center (RBDC): 700

**Your task is to develop an allocation plan for the NDRA.** Determine the optimal number of units for each defense resource type (Cybersecurity Analysts, Physical Security Personnel, Advanced Threat Detection Systems, and Network Redundancy Modules) to be assigned to each of the four strategic digital infrastructure locations (National Data Center, Primary Network Hub, Cloud Infrastructure Gateway, and Regional Backup Data Center). The primary objective is to **maximize the total weighted defense capability**. The contribution of each resource unit to this total defense capability is calculated by multiplying the number of units of that resource by the 'Defense Importance Score' of the location where it is deployed. For example, deploying one unit of Cybersecurity Analysts at the National Data Center contributes 10 * 1 = 10 to the total weighted defense capability.

Ensure that your allocation plan strictly adheres to the total availability of each resource type across all locations and that the total cost of resources deployed at each individual location does not exceed its specific allocated budget.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
A prominent Project Management Consulting Firm, 'ProjectGuard,' is facing increasing client churn in a highly competitive market. To proactively address this, ProjectGuard wants to develop more accurate and targeted churn prediction models for its diverse client base. Recognizing that different factors might be more predictive for different types of clients, the firm has categorized its clients into three distinct segments. For each segment, ProjectGuard aims to select a specific number of key data features from a larger pool of potential features to build a specialized churn prediction model.

ProjectGuard's data science and analytics team has provided expert estimates on the potential contribution of each candidate feature to the prediction accuracy of a churn model, specifically for each client segment. These contributions are measured on a proprietary scale, where higher values indicate a greater positive impact on model accuracy. To maintain model interpretability and computational efficiency, the firm has decided that exactly three features must be selected for each client segment's dedicated churn prediction model.

**Client Segments (I):**
1.  **SME (Small & Medium Enterprises):** Clients with smaller project portfolios and typically shorter engagement cycles.
2.  **LC (Large Corporations):** Clients undertaking complex, long-term, and high-value projects.
3.  **PSP (Public Sector Projects):** Government or public entity clients, often with strict regulatory requirements.

**Candidate Features (J):**
1.  **F1: Project Budget Adherence Score:** A metric reflecting how closely projects stay within their allocated budget (score 0-100).
2.  **F2: Client Engagement Frequency:** Average weekly interaction points (meetings, communication, feedback) with the client (score 0-100).
3.  **F3: Number of Scope Change Requests:** Total formal requests for project scope modifications from the client (score 0-100, lower implies better stability).
4.  **F4: Project Timeline Delay Index:** A normalized measure of average project delays for a client's projects (score 0-100, lower implies better punctuality).
5.  **F5: Post-Completion Satisfaction Rating:** Average client satisfaction score obtained from surveys after project completion (score 0-100).

**Estimated Contribution to Prediction Accuracy (w_ij values):**
Below is a matrix detailing the estimated contribution of each feature (F1-F5) to the churn prediction accuracy for each client segment (SME, LC, PSP). The values represent points of contribution.

| Feature \ Client Segment | SME | LC  | PSP |
| :----------------------- | :-- | :-- | :-- |
| F1: Budget Adherence     | 85  | 70  | 90  |
| F2: Client Engagement    | 90  | 80  | 60  |
| F3: Change Requests      | 75  | 95  | 85  |
| F4: Timeline Delay       | 80  | 85  | 70  |
| F5: Feedback Rating      | 60  | 75  | 90  |

**Optimization Goal:**
ProjectGuard's objective is to maximize the *total sum of prediction accuracy contributions* from the selected features across all three client segments, while adhering to the constraint of selecting exactly three features for each individual client segment. Determine which three features should be selected for each client segment (SME, LC, and PSP) to achieve this goal.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
## Numerical Problem: Dynamic Bandwidth Allocation in Telecommunication Services

This problem addresses the optimization of bandwidth allocation for **2 users** (indexed 1 and 2) over **2 distinct time periods** (indexed 0 and 1). The goal is to efficiently manage network resources and satisfy user demands while considering costs and service quality.

### Problem Background
In a telecommunications network serving two users over two time periods, effective bandwidth management is crucial. The network needs to dynamically adjust bandwidth allocation in real-time to adapt to changing demands and ensure cost-effectiveness and service quality.

### Optimization Objectives
The objective is to maximize a weighted combination of total utility and total cost. Specifically, we aim to:
Maximize: `1.0 * (Total Utility) - 0.5 * (Total Cost)`

Where:
*   **Total Utility** is the sum of utility obtained from allocating bandwidth to each user in each time period.
    *   Utility from User 1 in Time Period 0: `5` units per unit bandwidth.
    *   Utility from User 1 in Time Period 1: `4` units per unit bandwidth.
    *   Utility from User 2 in Time Period 0: `4` units per unit bandwidth.
    *   Utility from User 2 in Time Period 1: `5` units per unit bandwidth.
*   **Total Cost** is the sum of the costs of allocating bandwidth to each user in each time period.
    *   Cost for User 1 in Time Period 0: `1` unit per unit bandwidth.
    *   Cost for User 1 in Time Period 1: `2` units per unit bandwidth.
    *   Cost for User 2 in Time Period 0: `2` units per unit bandwidth.
    *   Cost for User 2 in Time Period 1: `1` unit per unit bandwidth.

### Decision Variables
Let `b[i, t]` represent the continuous amount of bandwidth allocated to user `i` in time period `t`.

### Problem Constraints

1.  **Bandwidth Resource Limitation:** The total bandwidth allocated in any given time period must not exceed the maximum capacity for that period.
    *   Maximum bandwidth capacity for Time Period 0: `100` units.
    *   Maximum bandwidth capacity for Time Period 1: `100` units.

    This translates to:
    *   `b[1, 0] + b[2, 0] <= 100` (for Time Period 0)
    *   `b[1, 1] + b[2, 1] <= 100` (for Time Period 1)

2.  **User Service Quality (QoS) Constraint:** Each user must receive at least a minimum required amount of bandwidth in each time period to meet their QoS standards.
    *   Minimum QoS for User 1: `10` units.
    *   Minimum QoS for User 2: `20` units.

    This translates to:
    *   `b[1, 0] >= 10`
    *   `b[1, 1] >= 10`
    *   `b[2, 0] >= 20`
    *   `b[2, 1] >= 20`

3.  **Cost Constraint:** The total cost of bandwidth allocation across all users and time periods must not exceed a predefined budget limit.
    *   Total budget limit: `300` units.

    This translates to:
    *   `(1 * b[1, 0] + 2 * b[1, 1]) + (2 * b[2, 0] + 1 * b[2, 1]) <= 300`

### Summary of Numerical Parameters

*   **Number of Users (M):** 2 (indexed 1, 2)
*   **Number of Time Periods:** 2 (indexed 0, 1)
*   **Maximum Bandwidth Capacity (`B_t`):**
    *   `B_0 = 100`
    *   `B_1 = 100`
*   **Minimum QoS Requirements (`Q_i`):**
    *   `Q_1 = 10`
    *   `Q_2 = 20`
*   **Cost of Unit Bandwidth Allocation (`C_it`):**
    *   `C_1,0 = 1`
    *   `C_1,1 = 2`
    *   `C_2,0 = 2`
    *   `C_2,1 = 1`
*   **Total Budget Limit (`C_max`):** `300`
*   **Utility Weight (`alpha`):** `1.0`
*   **Cost Weight (`beta`):** `0.5`
*   **Utility from Bandwidth Allocation (`U_it`):**
    *   `U_1,0 = 5`
    *   `U_1,1 = 4`
    *   `U_2,0 = 4`
    *   `U_2,1 = 5`

The problem seeks to find the optimal continuous bandwidth allocations `b[i, t]` for all users `i` and time periods `t` that maximize the weighted objective function while satisfying all specified constraints.
think step by step.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Agricultural Insurance Optimization Problem (Numerical Version)

Background
The agricultural insurance optimization problem involves how to reasonably design and price agricultural insurance products to reduce agricultural production risks, increase farmers' income, and achieve a balance between the profits and risk assumption of insurance companies. Effective agricultural insurance schemes can help farmers cope with uncontrollable factors such as natural disasters and climate change, ensuring the stability of food production.

This specific numerical instance considers two distinct agricultural insurance products, Product 1 and Product 2.

Decision Variables:
*   Let `x_i` be a binary variable, where `x_i = 1` if the farmer purchases agricultural insurance Product `i`, and `x_i = 0` otherwise.
*   Let `y_i` be a binary variable, where `y_i = 1` if the farmer receives compensation for agricultural insurance Product `i`, and `y_i = 0` otherwise.

Parameters:
*   For Product 1 (i=1):
    *   Maximum number of Product 1 a farmer can buy (`B_1`): 1
    *   Premium for Product 1 (`P_1`): 100 units
    *   Financial compensation amount received for Product 1 (`C_1`): 200 units
    *   Utility/Benefit for receiving compensation for Product 1 (`U_1`): 300 units
    *   Risk cost for buying Product 1 (`R_1`): 50 units
*   For Product 2 (i=2):
    *   Maximum number of Product 2 a farmer can buy (`B_2`): 1
    *   Premium for Product 2 (`P_2`): 150 units
    *   Financial compensation amount received for Product 2 (`C_2`): 250 units
    *   Utility/Benefit for receiving compensation for Product 2 (`U_2`): 400 units
    *   Risk cost for buying Product 2 (`R_2`): 60 units

Optimization Goals
The objective is to maximize the farmer's net utility, which is represented by the total benefit from receiving compensation minus the total risk cost associated with purchasing insurance products.
Maximize: `(300 * y_1 + 400 * y_2) - (50 * x_1 + 60 * x_2)`

Problem Constraints
The optimization must satisfy the following conditions:

1.  **Insurance purchase limit (Agricultural production risk constraints related to product availability):**
    Farmers can purchase at most one unit of each specific insurance product.
    *   `x_1 <= 1`
    *   `x_2 <= 1`

2.  **Insurance payout limitation (Insurance product type and limitation constraints):**
    Compensation for an insurance product can only be received if that product was actually purchased.
    *   `y_1 <= x_1`
    *   `y_2 <= x_2`

3.  **Farmers' economic status constraint:**
    The total premiums paid by the farmer must be greater than or equal to the total financial compensation received by the farmer. This implies that the farmer's net direct cash flow from the insurance products must be non-positive, focusing the benefit on the utility of risk reduction rather than direct cash profit from the transaction itself.
    *   `(100 * x_1 + 150 * x_2) - (200 * y_1 + 250 * y_2) >= 0`

All decision variables `x_1, x_2, y_1, y_2` are binary (0 or 1).

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization of Construction Plan in the Construction Industry
    Problem Background
    In the construction industry, the rational arrangement of construction plans is crucial for the successful completion of projects. This specific optimization problem aims to arrange two distinct construction tasks and allocate resources to them. The objective is to minimize the total construction cost, which is determined by the start times of these tasks. The arrangement must adhere to a logical dependency between the tasks and conform to basic resource availability limits.

    Optimization Goals
    - Minimize the total construction cost, which is directly influenced by the start times of the tasks.

    Decision Variables
    The problem involves two main types of decision variables:
    -   **t[0]**: A continuous variable representing the start time of Task 0.
    -   **t[1]**: A continuous variable representing the start time of Task 1.
    -   **x[0,0]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 0 utilizes Resource 0, and 0 otherwise.
    -   **x[0,1]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 1 utilizes Resource 0, and 0 otherwise.
    -   **x[1,0]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 0 utilizes Resource 1, and 0 otherwise.
    -   **x[1,1]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 1 utilizes Resource 1, and 0 otherwise.

    Parameters
    The problem involves the following numerical parameters:
    -   **Number of Tasks**: There are 2 tasks in consideration, referred to as Task 0 and Task 1.
    -   **Number of Resources**: There are 2 resources in consideration, referred to as Resource 0 and Resource 1.
    -   **Task Durations**:
        -   Task 0 has a duration of 3 time units.
        -   Task 1 has a duration of 2 time units.
    -   **Task Unit Time Costs**:
        -   The unit time cost associated with Task 0 is 100 monetary units.
        -   The unit time cost associated with Task 1 is 150 monetary units.
    -   **Resource Availability Limits**:
        -   The availability limit for Resource 0 is 1 unit.
        -   The availability limit for Resource 1 is 1 unit.

    Objective Function
    The objective is to minimize the total construction cost, calculated as the sum of the unit time costs multiplied by their respective task start times:
    Minimize: `100 * t[0] + 150 * t[1]`

    Problem Constraints
    The construction plan must satisfy the following constraints:
    -   **Task Dependency Constraint**: Task 1 cannot commence until Task 0 has been fully completed. Given that Task 0 has a duration of 3 time units, this dependency is formulated as:
        `t[1] >= t[0] + 3`
    -   **Resource Availability Constraints**: The assignment of tasks to resources must respect the maximum availability of each resource. For each Resource `i` (where `i` can be 0 or 1) and each Task `j` (where `j` can be 0 or 1), the binary variable `x[i,j]` (indicating if Task `j` uses Resource `i`) must be less than or equal to the availability limit of Resource `i`. Specifically, these constraints are:
        -   `x[0,0] <= 1` (Task 0's utilization of Resource 0 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
        -   `x[0,1] <= 1` (Task 1's utilization of Resource 0 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
        -   `x[1,0] <= 1` (Task 0's utilization of Resource 1 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
        -   `x[1,1] <= 1` (Task 1's utilization of Resource 1 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
    -   **Variable Type Constraints**:
        -   The decision variables `t[0]` and `t[1]` are continuous, meaning they can take any real value within their feasible range.
        -   The decision variables `x[0,0]`, `x[0,1]`, `x[1,0]`, and `x[1,1]` are binary, meaning they can only take values of 0 or 1.

TechInnovate Online, a rapidly expanding e-commerce company specializing in consumer electronics, is facing challenges in efficiently managing the inventory of its popular product, the 'NextGen SmartWatch'. To optimize their operations and minimize costs, the company needs a precise inventory plan for the upcoming 8 weeks.

At the beginning of Week 1, TechInnovate Online has an existing inventory of 40 units of the NextGen SmartWatch in its main warehouse. The company incurs two primary costs associated with inventory management:

1.  **Ordering Cost:** For each unit of NextGen SmartWatch ordered from their supplier, there is an associated cost of $7. This covers administrative processing, handling, and initial inspection upon arrival.
2.  **Holding Cost:** Storing each unit of the NextGen SmartWatch in the warehouse costs $3 per unit per week. This includes warehousing space, insurance, and potential obsolescence.

The marketing department has provided the following deterministic demand forecast for the NextGen SmartWatch over the next 8 weeks:

| Week | Forecasted Demand (Units) |
|------|---------------------------|
| 1    | 90                        |
| 2    | 110                       |
| 3    | 130                       |
| 4    | 100                       |
| 5    | 120                       |
| 6    | 140                       |
| 7    | 95                        |
| 8    | 125                       |

TechInnovate Online aims to develop an inventory strategy that satisfies all customer demand promptly while minimizing the total inventory-related costs (ordering and holding) over this 8-week planning horizon. All units ordered in a given week are assumed to be available to meet the demand within that same week. Additionally, the company cannot allow for any stockouts, meaning all demand must be met from available inventory, and inventory levels at the end of each week must be non-negative.

Your task is to determine the optimal quantity of NextGen SmartWatches to order in each of the 8 weeks and the resulting inventory level at the end of each week, such that the total ordering and holding costs are minimized over the entire planning period, subject to meeting all customer demand.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Charging Station Construction (Numerical Version)

**Problem Background**
The optimization problem of charging station construction involves how to reasonably allocate the location and number of charging stations in a region to meet the charging needs of electric vehicle users. This problem has practical application value in promoting the popularization of electric vehicles, improving the utilization rate of charging facilities, and reducing dependence on energy resources.

This specific numerical instance considers a region with 2 potential locations for charging station construction, indexed as 0 and 1.

**Decision Variables**
For each potential location `i` in the set `{0, 1}`, a binary decision variable `x[i]` is defined:
*   `x[i] = 1` if a charging station is built at location `i`.
*   `x[i] = 0` if a charging station is not built at location `i`.

**Parameters**
*   **User Demand (`a`):** The minimum number of charging stations required to meet the quantity needs of electric vehicle users in the region is `1`.
*   **Capacity Demand (`b`):** The minimum number of charging stations required to meet the overall charging station capacity needs in the region is `2`.
*   **Construction Costs (`c_construction`):**
    *   Construction cost for a charging station at location 0 is `3` units.
    *   Construction cost for a charging station at location 1 is `4` units.
*   **Operation Cost (`c_operation`):** The operating cost for any single charging station (if built) is `1` unit.

**Optimization Goals**
Minimize the total cost, which is composed of the construction costs and the operating costs for all built charging stations.
*   The objective function is defined as:
    Minimize `(3 * x[0] + 1) + (4 * x[1] + 1)`
    Which simplifies to:
    Minimize `3 * x[0] + 4 * x[1] + 2`

*   The goals of maximizing charging convenience for electric vehicle users and improving the utilization rate of charging stations and reducing user waiting time are addressed implicitly by the demand and capacity constraints, but are not explicitly quantified in the objective function with specific numerical terms in this formulation.

**Problem Constraints**
The optimization problem is subject to the following numerical constraints:

1.  **Electric Vehicle User Number Constraint:**
    The total number of charging stations built must be greater than or equal to the minimum requirement for electric vehicle users.
    `x[0] + x[1] >= 1`

2.  **Charging Station Capacity Constraint:**
    The total number of charging stations built must be greater than or equal to the minimum required capacity.
    `x[0] + x[1] >= 2`

*   The "Charging station location constraint" is implicitly handled by the definition of the available locations {0, 1} and the binary decision variables `x[i]`.
*   The "Charging equipment performance constraint" is assumed to be met by any station built and is not explicitly formulated with numerical values in the provided code.

The goal is to determine the binary values for `x[0]` and `x[1]` that minimize the total cost while satisfying all specified constraints.

A popular game development studio, "Nexus Games," is preparing for the highly anticipated launch of its new flagship role-playing game, "Aetheria Chronicles." To cater to different player preferences and budget levels, Nexus Games plans to release four distinct digital editions of the game. Each edition bundles the base game with various premium digital content and features, which consume specific, limited resources the studio has prepared.

The studio's production and development teams have finite capacity for certain high-value digital assets and services that are included in these special editions. Specifically, the following resources are limited:
*   **Unique In-Game Collectibles Slots**: The art and design teams have capacity to produce only **500** distinct digital collectible items (e.g., rare weapon skins, exclusive cosmetic armor sets) across all premium editions. Each collectible item provided in an edition consumes one "slot."
*   **Exclusive Early Access Slots**: The server infrastructure and support team can comfortably accommodate **300** players for an exclusive early access period before the official launch. Each player granted early access consumes one "slot."
*   **Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity**: The studio has the capacity to create and bundle **400** unique digital copies of a comprehensive Developer Diary and Art Book. Each digital copy included in an edition consumes one "slot."

Nexus Games has identified the following market demand and pricing for each edition, along with the specific premium resources they include:

1.  **Standard Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $50
    *   **Content**: Base Game.
    *   **Resource Consumption**: This edition does not include any of the above-mentioned premium unique collectibles, exclusive early access, or digital art books.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **15,000** units can be sold.

2.  **Deluxe Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $80
    *   **Content**: Base Game + 1 Unique In-Game Collectible + Digital Developer Diary & Art Book.
    *   **Resource Consumption**: Each Deluxe Edition sold consumes **1** Unique In-Game Collectible Slot and **1** Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity Slot.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **8,000** units can be sold.

3.  **Collector's Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $120
    *   **Content**: Base Game + 2 Unique In-Game Collectibles + Exclusive Early Access + Digital Developer Diary & Art Book.
    *   **Resource Consumption**: Each Collector's Edition sold consumes **2** Unique In-Game Collectible Slots, **1** Exclusive Early Access Slot, and **1** Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity Slot.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **3,000** units can be sold.

4.  **Ultimate Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $180
    *   **Content**: Base Game + 3 Unique In-Game Collectibles + Exclusive Early Access + Digital Developer Diary & Art Book + Season Pass (for all future DLCs).
    *   **Resource Consumption**: Each Ultimate Edition sold consumes **3** Unique In-Game Collectible Slots, **1** Exclusive Early Access Slot, and **1** Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity Slot.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **1,500** units can be sold.

Nexus Games' objective is to determine how many units of each game edition (Standard, Deluxe, Collector's, Ultimate) to sell to maximize their total revenue from the launch of "Aetheria Chronicles." The studio must ensure that they do not exceed the available capacity for any premium resource and also do not attempt to sell more units of any edition than its estimated market demand.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
A popular game development studio, "Nexus Games," is preparing for the highly anticipated launch of its new flagship role-playing game, "Aetheria Chronicles." To cater to different player preferences and budget levels, Nexus Games plans to release four distinct digital editions of the game. Each edition bundles the base game with various premium digital content and features, which consume specific, limited resources the studio has prepared.

The studio's production and development teams have finite capacity for certain high-value digital assets and services that are included in these special editions. Specifically, the following resources are limited:
*   **Unique In-Game Collectibles Slots**: The art and design teams have capacity to produce only **500** distinct digital collectible items (e.g., rare weapon skins, exclusive cosmetic armor sets) across all premium editions. Each collectible item provided in an edition consumes one "slot."
*   **Exclusive Early Access Slots**: The server infrastructure and support team can comfortably accommodate **300** players for an exclusive early access period before the official launch. Each player granted early access consumes one "slot."
*   **Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity**: The studio has the capacity to create and bundle **400** unique digital copies of a comprehensive Developer Diary and Art Book. Each digital copy included in an edition consumes one "slot."

Nexus Games has identified the following market demand and pricing for each edition, along with the specific premium resources they include:

1.  **Standard Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $50
    *   **Content**: Base Game.
    *   **Resource Consumption**: This edition does not include any of the above-mentioned premium unique collectibles, exclusive early access, or digital art books.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **15,000** units can be sold.

2.  **Deluxe Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $80
    *   **Content**: Base Game + 1 Unique In-Game Collectible + Digital Developer Diary & Art Book.
    *   **Resource Consumption**: Each Deluxe Edition sold consumes **1** Unique In-Game Collectible Slot and **1** Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity Slot.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **8,000** units can be sold.

3.  **Collector's Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $120
    *   **Content**: Base Game + 2 Unique In-Game Collectibles + Exclusive Early Access + Digital Developer Diary & Art Book.
    *   **Resource Consumption**: Each Collector's Edition sold consumes **2** Unique In-Game Collectible Slots, **1** Exclusive Early Access Slot, and **1** Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity Slot.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **3,000** units can be sold.

4.  **Ultimate Edition**:
    *   **Price**: $180
    *   **Content**: Base Game + 3 Unique In-Game Collectibles + Exclusive Early Access + Digital Developer Diary & Art Book + Season Pass (for all future DLCs).
    *   **Resource Consumption**: Each Ultimate Edition sold consumes **3** Unique In-Game Collectible Slots, **1** Exclusive Early Access Slot, and **1** Developer Diary & Art Book Production Capacity Slot.
    *   **Estimated Market Demand**: A maximum of **1,500** units can be sold.

Nexus Games' objective is to determine how many units of each game edition (Standard, Deluxe, Collector's, Ultimate) to sell to maximize their total revenue from the launch of "Aetheria Chronicles." The studio must ensure that they do not exceed the available capacity for any premium resource and also do not attempt to sell more units of any edition than its estimated market demand.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
EcoServe Logistics, a company committed to sustainable practices, operates two production facilities (Facility A and Facility B) and serves three major customer regions (Region 1, Region 2, and Region 3). The company manufactures a single type of sustainable product. EcoServe Logistics aims to optimize its production and distribution network to meet all customer demands at the lowest possible total cost, considering not only operational expenses but also environmental impacts. 

Here is the relevant data for their operations for the upcoming month:

**1. Production Facility Details:**

| Facility | Monthly Production Capacity (units) | Production Cost per Unit ($) | Environmental Cost per Unit ($) |
| :------- | :--------------------------------- | :--------------------------- | :------------------------------ |
| A        | 8,000                              | 15                           | 3                               |
| B        | 12,000                             | 18                           | 1                               |

*Note: The Environmental Cost per Unit reflects the cost associated with the carbon footprint and other environmental externalities generated during the production of one unit at that facility. EcoServe Logistics internalizes these costs as part of its sustainability commitment.*

**2. Customer Demand Details:**

| Customer Region | Monthly Demand (units) |
| :-------------- | :--------------------- |
| Region 1        | 5,000                  |
| Region 2        | 6,000                  |
| Region 3        | 4,000                  |

**3. Transportation Costs per Unit:**

| From Facility \ To Customer Region | Region 1 ($) | Region 2 ($) | Region 3 ($) |
| :-------------------------------- | :----------- | :----------- | :----------- |
| A                                 | 5            | 8            | 6            |
| B                                 | 7            | 4            | 5            |

EcoServe Logistics needs to determine an optimal plan for how many units to produce at each facility and how many units to ship from each facility to each customer region. The primary goal is to minimize the company's total supply chain cost, which includes all production costs, environmental costs, and transportation costs.

Your task is to develop a plan that specifies:

1.  The total quantity of product to be manufactured at each Facility A and Facility B.
2.  The quantity of product to be shipped from each facility to each of the three customer regions.

This plan must ensure that:
*   All customer demands in Region 1, Region 2, and Region 3 are fully satisfied.
*   The production at each facility does not exceed its stated monthly capacity.
*   The total units shipped from a facility match the total units produced at that facility.
*   All quantities for production and shipment are non-negative.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Agricultural Waste Disposal

Problem Background
The optimization of agricultural waste disposal involves how to effectively deal with the waste generated in agricultural production. There are two types of agricultural waste, referred to as Waste Type 1 and Waste Type 2, which need to be processed at two available disposal facilities, Facility 1 and Facility 2. A reasonable waste disposal scheme aims to reduce environmental pollution, improve resource utilization efficiency, and minimize the cost of waste disposal.

Optimization Objectives
The objective is to minimize the total cost, which includes the cost of processing waste at facilities, a penalty cost associated with the environmental impact of emissions, and a cost for any waste that is not processed.
Specifically, the objective function is to minimize:
`(5 + 1) * x[1,1] + (6 + 2) * x[1,2] + (7 + 3) * x[2,1] + (8 + 4) * x[2,2] + 10 * w[1] + 12 * w[2]`
where:
- `x[i,j]` represents the quantity of Waste Type `i` processed at Facility `j`.
- `w[i]` represents the quantity of Waste Type `i` that is not processed.
- The values `5, 6, 7, 8` are the unit processing costs for `x[1,1], x[1,2], x[2,1], x[2,2]` respectively.
- The values `1, 2, 3, 4` are the emission factors per unit of waste processed for `x[1,1], x[1,2], x[2,1], x[2,2]` respectively, treated as a cost in the objective function.
- The values `10` and `12` are the costs per unit for not processing Waste Type 1 and Waste Type 2, respectively.

Problem Constraints
The waste disposal scheme must adhere to the following constraints:

1.  **Waste Generation Constraints (Waste Balance):** The total quantity of each waste type processed at all facilities plus the quantity of that waste type left unprocessed must equal the total generated quantity of that waste type.
    *   For Waste Type 1: `x[1,1] + x[1,2] + w[1] == 10` (where `10` is the generated quantity of Waste Type 1).
    *   For Waste Type 2: `x[2,1] + x[2,2] + w[2] == 20` (where `20` is the generated quantity of Waste Type 2).

2.  **Disposal Facility Capacity Constraints:** The total quantity of waste processed at each facility cannot exceed its specific processing capacity.
    *   For Facility 1: `x[1,1] + x[2,1] <= 15` (where `15` is the processing capacity of Facility 1).
    *   For Facility 2: `x[1,2] + x[2,2] <= 25` (where `25` is the processing capacity of Facility 2).

3.  **Environmental Emission Standard Constraints:** The total environmental emissions generated from all waste processing activities must not exceed a specified maximum acceptable level.
    *   Total Emissions: `(1 * x[1,1]) + (2 * x[1,2]) + (3 * x[2,1]) + (4 * x[2,2]) <= 50` (where `50` is the maximum acceptable total emissions).
    *   The values `1, 2, 3, 4` are the emission factors per unit of waste processed for `x[1,1], x[1,2], x[2,1], x[2,2]` respectively.

4.  **Non-negativity Constraints:** All decision variables `x[i,j]` and `w[i]` must be non-negative continuous values.

The Dean of the College of Arts and Sciences at a university is planning for the upcoming academic year and needs to allocate a limited pool of student staff members to various essential academic support initiatives. The goal is to staff these initiatives effectively while minimizing the total cost incurred by the college.

There are a total of 50 qualified student staff members available for deployment across all initiatives. Each initiative requires a specific set of skills, and thus a minimum number of staff positions to ensure its successful operation. The cost associated with assigning a student staff member varies slightly depending on the nature of the initiative, reflecting different levels of required expertise or hourly commitments.

Here are the details for the five key academic support initiatives:

1.  **Undergraduate Research Mentorship Program (URMP)**:
    *   **Cost per staff member**: $2,500 for the academic year.

    *   **Cost per staff member**: $2,000 for the academic year.

3.  **IT Support for Digital Classrooms (ITS)**:
    *   **Cost per staff member**: $2,200 for the academic year.
    *   **Skill Requirements**: A minimum of 6 staff positions are essential for roles requiring advanced Technical Troubleshooting skills for classroom technology, and 2 additional staff positions are needed for roles focused on Network Configuration and AV setup.

4.  **Community Outreach & Engagement Events (COEE)**:
    *   **Cost per staff member**: $1,800 for the academic year.
    *   **Skill Requirements**: A minimum of 4 staff positions are needed for roles involving Event Planning & Logistics, and 3 staff positions are required for roles focused on Public Relations and community liaison activities.

5.  **Departmental Archiving & Digitization Project (DADP)**:
    *   **Cost per staff member**: $1,900 for the academic year.
    *   **Skill Requirements**: A minimum of 5 staff positions are crucial for roles demanding meticulous Data Entry skills for historical records, and 2 staff positions are needed for roles requiring Digital Asset Management skills.

The Dean's objective is to determine the number of student staff members to assign to each of the five initiatives such that the total staffing cost for the academic year is minimized. This allocation must ensure that each initiative meets its specified minimum staff requirements based on combined skill needs, and the total number of student staff deployed does not exceed the available pool of 50 individuals.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Agricultural Veterinary Scheduling and Planning

    Problem Background
    The optimization of agricultural veterinary scheduling and planning involves how to effectively arrange the work schedule of veterinarians to meet the health needs of farm animals. There are **2** farms (Farm 0 and Farm 1) and a limited number of veterinarians. Specifically, there are **2** veterinarians (Veterinarian 0 and Veterinarian 1) available for scheduling. The planning horizon is divided into **2** discrete time slots (Time Slot 0 and Time Slot 1). The goal is to reasonably schedule the time and resources of these **2** veterinarians to ensure animal health and improve the efficiency of veterinary services for the **2** farms over the **2** time slots.

    Optimization Goals
    The primary goal is to maximize the total net benefit derived from veterinarian visits. This net benefit is calculated by considering the health benefits gained from visits and the costs incurred.
    - Maximize the health status of farm animals: Each visit by any veterinarian to any farm at any time slot contributes a uniform health benefit of **10** units.
    - Optimize the scheduling plan of veterinarians to improve work efficiency: This is implicitly addressed by maximizing the net benefit.
    - Minimize the route of veterinary rounds to reduce costs: Each visit by any veterinarian to any farm incurs a uniform patrol cost of **5** units.
    The combined objective is to maximize the sum of `(10 * x[i, j, t] - 5 * D[j] * x[i, j, t])` for all veterinarians `i` in `{0, 1}`, farms `j` in `{0, 1}`, and time slots `t` in `{0, 1}`. Given that the health demand parameter `D[j]` is **1** for both farms, this objective simplifies to maximizing `(10 - 5) * x[i, j, t] = 5 * x[i, j, t]` for each visit, meaning the total objective is to maximize the sum of **5** for every visit made.

    Problem Constraints
    - Veterinarian number constraint: At any given farm (Farm 0 or Farm 1) and any given time slot (Time Slot 0 or Time Slot 1), the maximum number of veterinarians that can be present simultaneously is **2**.
    - Animal health needs constraint: Animals on each farm have specific health needs. Farm 0 requires a total of at least **1** visit (from any veterinarian across all time slots), and Farm 1 also requires a total of at least **1** visit (from any veterinarian across all time slots).
    - Rounds time window constraint: Each veterinarian (Veterinarian 0 or Veterinarian 1) in each time slot (Time Slot 0 or Time Slot 1) must be assigned to visit exactly one farm (Farm 0 or Farm 1). This ensures that a veterinarian is uniquely occupied at a specific farm during each time slot and cannot be in multiple places at once.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
CityLink Communications is responsible for maintaining critical network infrastructure across a metropolitan area. To ensure network reliability, a field technician is assigned to perform routine checks and minor maintenance at several key network nodes daily. The technician starts their day at the central depot, must visit each assigned network node exactly once, and then return to the central depot to conclude their shift.

The operations team aims to optimize the technician's route to minimize the total travel time, thereby improving efficiency and allowing for more tasks to be completed or reducing operational costs. For today's shift, the technician needs to visit six specific network nodes. The estimated travel times (in minutes) between the central depot and these nodes, as well as between each pair of nodes, are provided in the table below. These times account for typical traffic conditions during operational hours.

**Locations to Visit:**
*   Central Depot (D)
*   Network Node A (NA)
*   Network Node B (NB)
*   Network Node C (NC)
*   Network Node D (ND)
*   Network Node E (NE)
*   Network Node F (NF)

**Estimated Travel Times (in minutes) between Locations:**

| From / To | D  | NA | NB | NC | ND | NE | NF |
| :-------- | :- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- |
| D         | -  | 15 | 20 | 10 | 25 | 18 | 22 |
| NA        | 15 | -  | 12 | 25 | 10 | 14 | 20 |
| NB        | 20 | 12 | -  | 18 | 22 | 8  | 15 |
| NC        | 10 | 25 | 18 | -  | 15 | 20 | 12 |
| ND        | 25 | 10 | 22 | 15 | -  | 16 | 11 |
| NE        | 18 | 14 | 8  | 20 | 16 | -  | 13 |
| NF        | 22 | 20 | 15 | 12 | 11 | 13 | -  |


**Your Task:**
Determine the optimal sequence of visits for the technician to minimize the total travel time for their complete tour. The tour must start at the Central Depot, visit each of the six network nodes exactly once, and end back at the Central Depot.

**Objective:** Minimize the total travel time for the technician's route.

**Requirements:**
1.  Identify the complete tour, listing the sequence of locations visited (e.g., D -> NA -> NB -> ... -> D).
2.  Calculate the total travel time for this determined tour.
3.  Ensure that each network node (NA, NB, NC, ND, NE, NF) is visited exactly once.
4.  The tour must begin and end at the Central Depot (D).

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
A leading Big Data Analytics company is re-evaluating its data distribution network to optimize service delivery and operational costs. The company operates two primary data centers and is considering establishing regional data hubs to efficiently serve its client zones. The goal is to design an optimal network configuration that minimizes total costs while meeting client demands and respecting operational capacities.

**Primary Data Centers:**
The company has two primary data centers with the following processing and outgoing data capacities:
*   Data Center A: Maximum outgoing data capacity of 500 Terabytes (TB) per day.
*   Data Center B: Maximum outgoing data capacity of 300 Terabytes (TB) per day.

**Potential Regional Data Hub Locations:**
There are three potential locations for establishing regional data hubs. Each hub incurs a fixed setup cost if opened, and has a maximum data throughput capacity:
*   Regional Data Hub 1: Setup cost $50,000, maximum daily throughput capacity of 400 TB.
*   Regional Data Hub 2: Setup cost $40,000, maximum daily throughput capacity of 350 TB.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Park Site Selection Planning Optimization Problem
Problem Background
Park site selection planning involves finding the best location in the city to build a park. For this problem, there are **two potential park locations**, designated as Location 1 and Location 2. The goal is to provide leisure and entertainment venues, improve the quality of life for residents, and meet the requirements of urban greening and planning. This problem requires a comprehensive consideration of factors such as land use, resident needs, and transportation convenience to achieve scientific and reasonable planning for park site selection.

Optimization Goals
The objective is to **maximize** a combined score that reflects the benefits and costs. Specifically:
- **Maximize the service range of the park, benefiting more residents:** Each unit of service range provided by a park at Location 1 contributes **10 units** to the objective, and each unit of service range from Location 2 contributes **15 units**.
- **Optimize park site selection, improving the level of urban greening:** This is achieved by deciding which locations to build parks.
- **Consider factors such as land cost and transportation convenience to ensure the feasibility of the site selection:** Building a park at Location 1 incurs a cost of **5 units**, and building a park at Location 2 incurs a cost of **8 units**. Additionally, there is a penalty for any unmet resident demand, with each unit of unmet demand reducing the objective by **2 units**.

Problem Constraints
- **Land use planning constraints:** The decision to build a park at a given location is a binary choice (either build or not build).
- **Resident needs constraints:** The total service range provided by all selected parks, combined with any unmet demand, must be at least the total resident demand. The resident demand for the area served by Location 1 is **30 units**, and for Location 2 is **40 units**. Therefore, the total service provided plus unmet demand must be at least **70 units**.
- **Transportation convenience constraints:** For each potential location, a traffic accessibility factor is considered. For Location 1, this factor is **0.5**, and for Location 2, it is **0.7**. If a park is selected at a location, its traffic accessibility factor multiplied by the selection decision must be non-negative.
- **Service range linking constraints:** The service range provided by a park at a specific location can only be non-zero if a park is actually built at that location. If a park is not built at a location, its service range must be zero. If a park is built, its service range can be up to a large number (e.g., **100** units).
- All service range values and unmet demand must be non-negative.

## Scientific Research Initiative: Optimizing Task Allocation and Scheduling

A leading biomedical research institute is launching a critical new initiative focused on developing novel diagnostics for a prevalent disease. This initiative involves a series of interconnected research tasks that must be completed efficiently by a multidisciplinary team within a tight 5-day work week, starting on Monday and concluding on Friday. ### Research Team Members and Capacities:
The research team consists of four key members, each with varying expertise and weekly task capacities:

1.  **Dr. Anya Sharma (Senior Researcher):** Highly experienced in experimental design and data interpretation. Can oversee a maximum of **4 tasks** during the 5-day week.
2.  **Dr. Ben Carter (Post-doctoral Fellow):** Skilled across various lab techniques and data analysis. Can undertake a maximum of **5 tasks** during the 5-day week.
3.  **Carly Davis (PhD Student):** Proficient in lab procedures and basic bioinformatics. Can undertake a maximum of **5 tasks** during the 5-day week.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Community Policing Patrol (Numerical Instance)

This problem focuses on optimizing community policing patrol for a specific scenario involving **2 community areas** (indexed as 0 and 1) and **2 patrol units** (indexed as 0 and 1). The goal is to determine which community areas each patrol unit should cover to maximize overall effectiveness.

**Decision Variables:**
We define binary decision variables, `Patrol_ij`, for `i \in \{0, 1\}` and `j \in \{0, 1\}`:
*   `Patrol_ij = 1` if patrol unit `j` is assigned to cover community area `i`.
*   `Patrol_ij = 0` otherwise.

Specifically, the decision variables are:
*   `Patrol_00`: Patrol unit 0 covers community area 0.
*   `Patrol_01`: Patrol unit 1 covers community area 0.
*   `Patrol_10`: Patrol unit 0 covers community area 1.
*   `Patrol_11`: Patrol unit 1 covers community area 1.

**Optimization Objective:**
The objective is to maximize a weighted sum of coverage and response time, where `Coverage_ij` represents the benefit of patrol unit `j` covering community area `i`, and `ResponseTime_ij` represents a penalty for the response time of patrol unit `j` in community area `i`.

The numerical values for these parameters are:
*   `Coverage = [[2, 3], [1, 2]]` (i.e., `Coverage_00=2, Coverage_01=3, Coverage_10=1, Coverage_11=2`)
*   `ResponseTime = [[1, 2], [2, 3]]` (i.e., `ResponseTime_00=1, ResponseTime_01=2, ResponseTime_10=2, ResponseTime_11=3`)

The objective function to be maximized is:
$$
\text{Maximize } \sum_{i=0}^{1} \sum_{j=0}^{1} (\text{Coverage}_{ij} - \text{ResponseTime}_{ij}) \cdot \text{Patrol}_{ij}
$$
Substituting the numerical values:
$$
\text{Maximize } (2-1)\cdot\text{Patrol}_{00} + (3-2)\cdot\text{Patrol}_{01} + (1-2)\cdot\text{Patrol}_{10} + (2-3)\cdot\text{Patrol}_{11}
$$
$$
\text{Maximize } 1\cdot\text{Patrol}_{00} + 1\cdot\text{Patrol}_{01} - 1\cdot\text{Patrol}_{10} - 1\cdot\text{Patrol}_{11}
$$

**Problem Constraints:**

1.  **Community Boundary Constraint:** Ensure patrol unit `j` only covers community area `i` if it is within its designated boundary.
    The numerical values for `Boundary_ij` are: `Boundary = [[1, 1], [1, 1]]`.
    $$
    \text{Patrol}_{ij} \leq \text{Boundary}_{ij}, \quad \forall i \in \{0, 1\}, j \in \{0, 1\}
    $$
    *   `Patrol_00 \leq 1`
    *   `Patrol_01 \leq 1`
    *   `Patrol_10 \leq 1`
    *   `Patrol_11 \leq 1`
    (Note: These constraints are redundant given `Patrol_ij` are binary variables, but are explicitly included in the model.)

2.  **Patrol Time Constraint:** Limit the total time spent by each patrol unit across all community areas it covers.
    The numerical values for `Duration_i` (time to cover community area `i`) are: `Duration = [2, 3]` (i.e., `Duration_0=2, Duration_1=3`).
    The numerical values for `MaxPatrolTime_j` (maximum time for patrol unit `j`) are: `MaxPatrolTime = [4, 5]` (i.e., `MaxPatrolTime_0=4, MaxPatrolTime_1=5`).
    $$
    \sum_{i=0}^{1} \text{Patrol}_{ij} \cdot \text{Duration}_{i} \leq \text{MaxPatrolTime}_{j}, \quad \forall j \in \{0, 1\}
    $$
    *   For patrol unit `j=0`: `Patrol_00 \cdot 2 + Patrol_10 \cdot 3 \leq 4`
    *   For patrol unit `j=1`: `Patrol_01 \cdot 2 + Patrol_11 \cdot 3 \leq 5`

3.  **Emergency Response Constraint:** Ensure that at least one patrol unit is assigned to each community area.
    $$
    \sum_{j=0}^{1} \text{Patrol}_{ij} \geq 1, \quad \forall i \in \{0, 1\}
    $$
    *   For community area `i=0`: `Patrol_00 + Patrol_01 \geq 1`
    *   For community area `i=1`: `Patrol_10 + Patrol_11 \geq 1`

4.  **Dynamic Adjustment Constraint (Business Constraint 1):** This constraint is intended for dynamic adjustments.
    The numerical values for `DynamicFactor_ij` are: `DynamicFactor = [[1, 1], [1, 1]]`.
    $$
    \text{DynamicFactor}_{ij} \cdot \text{Patrol}_{ij} = \text{Patrol}_{ij}, \quad \forall i \in \{0, 1\}, j \in \{0, 1\}
    $$
    *   `1 \cdot Patrol_00 = Patrol_00`
    *   `1 \cdot Patrol_01 = Patrol_01`
    *   `1 \cdot Patrol_10 = Patrol_10`
    *   `1 \cdot Patrol_11 = Patrol_11`
    (Note: With the current `DynamicFactor` values set to 1, these constraints are always true and effectively do not restrict the solution space.)

5.  **Minimum Patrol Frequency Constraint (Business Constraint 2):** Ensure each community area meets a minimum patrol frequency.
    The numerical values for `Frequency_j` (frequency of patrol unit `j`) are: `Frequency = [1, 1]` (i.e., `Frequency_0=1, Frequency_1=1`).
    The numerical values for `MinPatrolFrequency_i` (minimum required frequency for community area `i`) are: `MinPatrolFrequency = [1, 1]` (i.e., `MinPatrolFrequency_0=1, MinPatrolFrequency_1=1`).
    $$
    \sum_{j=0}^{1} \text{Patrol}_{ij} \cdot \text{Frequency}_{j} \geq \text{MinPatrolFrequency}_{i}, \quad \forall i \in \{0, 1\}
    $$
    *   For community area `i=0`: `Patrol_00 \cdot 1 + Patrol_01 \cdot 1 \geq 1`
    *   For community area `i=1`: `Patrol_10 \cdot 1 + Patrol_11 \cdot 1 \geq 1`
    (Note: With the current `Frequency` and `MinPatrolFrequency` values, these constraints are identical to the Emergency Response Constraints.)
think step by step.

A power utility company, operating within the coal industry, needs to develop an optimal power generation schedule for the next 5 hours (Hour 1 to Hour 5) to meet anticipated electricity demand while minimizing total costs. The company has three coal-fired power generation units, named Unit A, Unit B, and Unit C, with distinct operational characteristics. All units are initially offline (off) at the beginning of Hour 1.

Each unit has specific operational parameters:

| Unit  | Minimum Output (MW) | Maximum Output (MW) | Base Operating Cost ($/hour when online) | Cost per MWh ($/MWh) | Startup Cost ($) |
| :---- | :------------------ | :------------------ | :--------------------------------------- | :------------------- | :--------------- |
| Unit A| 20                  | 100                 | 500                                      | 15                   | 1000             |
| Unit B| 30                  | 150                 | 700                                      | 12                   | 1200             |
| Unit C| 10                  | 80                  | 300                                      | 20                   | 800              |

The anticipated electricity demand for each of the 5 hours is as follows:

| Hour  | Demand (MW) |
| :---- | :---------- |
| Hour 1| 120         |
| Hour 2| 180         |
| Hour 3| 200         |
| Hour 4| 160         |
| Hour 5| 130         |

The company must adhere to the following operational rules and constraints:

1.  **Demand Satisfaction:** The total power generated by all online units in any given hour must meet or exceed the electricity demand for that hour.
2.  **Unit Output Limits:** For any unit that is committed (turned on) in a given hour, its power output must be within its specified minimum and maximum output capacities. An offline unit produces zero power.
3.  **Reserve Capacity:** In each hour, the total maximum generation capacity of all committed units must be at least 15% greater than the actual electricity demand for that hour. This ensures a sufficient reserve to handle unexpected demand fluctuations or outages.
4.  **Startup Costs:** A startup cost is incurred for a unit in any hour it is brought online (i.e., if it was offline in the previous hour or at the beginning of Hour 1, and is online in the current hour).

Your task is to determine the optimal commitment schedule for each unit (i.e., which units are on or off in each hour) and the optimal power output for each online unit in each hour. The objective is to minimize the total cost, which includes the base operating costs for all online units, the variable generation costs based on MWh produced, and any incurred startup costs, over the entire 5-hour planning horizon.

Develop a detailed power generation plan, specifying for each hour and each unit whether it is online or offline, and if online, its power output in MW. Also, calculate the total cost for the entire 5-hour period under your optimal plan.

To optimize its operations and minimize overall costs, Elegance Timepieces needs to determine the optimal flow of components from suppliers to assembly plants, the production of watches at these plants, and the subsequent distribution to its retailers. The ultimate goal is to meet all customer demand precisely on time while adhering to operational capacities.

The objective is to minimize the total cost incurred across the supply chain over the three-month planning horizon. This total cost includes transportation costs for components from suppliers to manufacturers, transportation costs for finished luxury watches from manufacturers to retailers, and the costs of holding inventory at both the assembly plants and retail boutiques.

Here is the detailed information required for planning:

*   **Suppliers (S):** S1 (specialized watch movements), S2 (precious metal casings)

    *   S1: 80 units

*   **Manufacturer Production Capacity (maximum units M can assemble):**
    *   M1: 70 units
    *   M2: 60 units

**5. Initial Conditions:**
   Assume zero initial inventory at all manufacturers (M1, M2) and retailers (R1, R2, R3) at the beginning of Month 1.

**Problem Requirements:**

This plan must minimize the total combined transportation and inventory holding costs over the three-month planning horizon, while ensuring all retailer demands are met and all capacity constraints are respected. Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
**Numerical Problem Description**

**Problem Background**
In a specific military intelligence gathering scenario, there are **2 distinct intelligence gathering tasks** (referred to as Task 0 and Task 1) that need to be optimized for execution. There are **2 types of resources** (referred to as Resource 0 and Resource 1) available to perform these tasks. The objective is to allocate these resources to tasks to maximize the overall benefit, considering their respective intelligence values, risks, and resource limitations.

**Optimization Objectives**
The goal is to maximize a combined objective function that prioritizes high intelligence value while penalizing high risk. Specifically, we aim to:
1.  **Maximize the total value of key intelligence gathered:** Each unit of intelligence gathered from Task 0 contributes **10 units** of value, and from Task 1 contributes **15 units** of value.
2.  **Minimize the total risk of intelligence gathering missions:** Each execution of Task 0 incurs **2 units** of risk, and Task 1 incurs **3 units** of risk.
3.  **Optimize resource usage:** This is implicitly handled by the resource availability constraints.

The overall objective function to be maximized is:
`(1 * (10 * (x[0,0] + x[1,0]) + 15 * (x[0,1] + x[1,1]))) - (1 * (2*x[0,0] + 3*x[0,1] + 2*x[1,0] + 3*x[1,1]))`
where `x[i,j]` is a binary decision variable indicating if Resource `i` is assigned to Task `j`. The intelligence value is weighted by `1` and the risk is weighted by `1`.

**Decision Variables**
Binary variables `x[i, j]` are defined for `i` in `{0, 1}` (representing Resource 0 and Resource 1) and `j` in `{0, 1}` (representing Task 0 and Task 1). `x[i, j] = 1` if resource `i` is assigned to task `j`, and `0` otherwise.

**Problem Constraints**
1.  **Resource Availability Constraint:**
    *   Resource 0 has an availability limit allowing it to be assigned to at most **3 tasks**. This is formulated as: `x[0,0] + x[0,1] <= 3`.
    *   Resource 1 has an availability limit allowing it to be assigned to at most **2 tasks**. This is formulated as: `x[1,0] + x[1,1] <= 2`.
2.  **Risk Management Constraint:** The total risk incurred by any single resource must not exceed a preset safety threshold of **5 units**.
    *   For Resource 0: `2*x[0,0] + 3*x[0,1] <= 5`.
    *   For Resource 1: `2*x[1,0] + 3*x[1,1] <= 5`.
3.  **Operation Time Window Constraint:** Due to specific operational timing restrictions, Resource 0 **cannot be assigned to Task 1**. This is enforced by: `x[0,1] == 0`.
4.  **Binary Constraints:** All decision variables `x[i,j]` must be binary.

**Note:** The current model instance does not explicitly incorporate "Task dependency constraint" or a general "Target coverage constraint" (beyond what the objective implicitly drives) as described in the original symbolic problem. The "Operation time window constraint" is represented by a single, specific restriction rather than a general framework.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Construction Site Material Procurement - Numerical Instance

Problem Background
In a construction project, the effective procurement of building materials is crucial. This specific instance focuses on procuring 2 types of building materials from 2 available suppliers. The goal is to obtain the required materials at the lowest possible cost while ensuring quality standards are met within a limited budget and supplier capacities.

Optimization Goals
The primary objective is to minimize the total cost, which includes both the direct procurement cost and any penalties incurred for not meeting specified quality standards.

Problem Entities and Parameters:
*   **Suppliers**: There are 2 available suppliers, indexed as Supplier 1 and Supplier 2.
*   **Building Materials**: There are 2 types of building materials required, indexed as Material 1 and Material 2.

*   **Availability Resource Consumption (`w`)**: This matrix defines the amount of "availability resource" (e.g., time, capacity units) consumed by procuring a unit of material from a specific supplier.
    *   Procuring Material 1 from Supplier 1 consumes 2 units of resource.
    *   Procuring Material 2 from Supplier 1 consumes 3 units of resource.
    *   Procuring Material 1 from Supplier 2 consumes 1 unit of resource.
    *   Procuring Material 2 from Supplier 2 consumes 4 units of resource.

*   **Supplier Availability Resource Capacity (`T`)**: This vector specifies the total availability resource capacity for each supplier.
    *   Supplier 1 has a total resource capacity of 5 units.
    *   Supplier 2 has a total resource capacity of 6 units.

*   **Unit Cost (`c`)**: This matrix defines the unit cost of procuring each material from each supplier.
    *   Unit cost for Material 1 from Supplier 1 is 4.
    *   Unit cost for Material 2 from Supplier 1 is 5.
    *   Unit cost for Material 1 from Supplier 2 is 6.
    *   Unit cost for Material 2 from Supplier 2 is 7.

*   **Budget (`B`)**: The total procurement budget is 20.

*   **Quality Rating (`q`)**: This matrix provides the quality rating for each material if procured from a specific supplier.
    *   Quality rating for Material 1 from Supplier 1 is 8.
    *   Quality rating for Material 2 from Supplier 1 is 9.
    *   Quality rating for Material 1 from Supplier 2 is 7.
    *   Quality rating for Material 2 from Supplier 2 is 10.

*   **Minimum Quality Standard (`Q`)**: This vector specifies the minimum acceptable total quality rating for each material type, aggregated across all chosen suppliers.
    *   Minimum quality standard for Material 1 is 15.
    *   Minimum quality standard for Material 2 is 18.

*   **Quality Shortfall Penalty (`p`)**: This vector defines the penalty cost for each unit of quality shortfall for each material type.
    *   Penalty for 1 unit of quality shortfall for Material 1 is 1.
    *   Penalty for 1 unit of quality shortfall for Material 2 is 1.

Decision Variables
*   `x[i, j]`: A binary variable, where `x[i, j] = 1` if Material `j` is procured from Supplier `i`, and `0` otherwise.
    *   `x[1,1]`: Procure Material 1 from Supplier 1.
    *   `x[1,2]`: Procure Material 2 from Supplier 1.
    *   `x[2,1]`: Procure Material 1 from Supplier 2.
    *   `x[2,2]`: Procure Material 2 from Supplier 2.
*   `s[j]`: A non-negative continuous variable representing the shortfall in the total quality rating for Material `j` below its minimum required standard.
    *   `s[1]`: Quality shortfall for Material 1.
    *   `s[2]`: Quality shortfall for Material 2.

Objective Function
Minimize the total cost, which is the sum of the procurement costs and the penalties for quality shortfalls:
Minimize: `(4 * x[1,1] + 5 * x[1,2] + 6 * x[2,1] + 7 * x[2,2]) + (1 * s[1] + 1 * s[2])`

Constraints
1.  **Supplier Availability Constraints**: The total availability resource consumed by procuring materials from each supplier must not exceed that supplier's capacity.
    *   For Supplier 1: `2 * x[1,1] + 3 * x[1,2] <= 5`
    *   For Supplier 2: `1 * x[2,1] + 4 * x[2,2] <= 6`

2.  **Procurement Budget Constraint**: The total cost of procured materials must not exceed the budget.
    *   `4 * x[1,1] + 5 * x[1,2] + 6 * x[2,1] + 7 * x[2,2] <= 20`

3.  **Building Material Quality Standard Constraints**: The sum of quality ratings for each material type from selected suppliers, plus any quality shortfall `s[j]`, must meet or exceed the minimum quality standard for that material.
    *   For Material 1: `8 * x[1,1] + 7 * x[2,1] + s[1] >= 15`
    *   For Material 2: `9 * x[1,2] + 10 * x[2,2] + s[2] >= 18`

4.  **Variable Type Constraints**:
    *   `x[i,j]` are binary variables (0 or 1).
    *   `s[j]` are non-negative continuous variables (`s[j] >= 0`).

1.  **Supplier Availability Constraints**: The total availability resource consumed by procuring materials from each supplier must not exceed that supplier's capacity.
    *   For Supplier 1: `2 * x[1,1] + 3 * x[1,2] <= 5`
    *   For Supplier 2: `1 * x[2,1] + 4 * x[2,2] <= 6`

2.  **Procurement Budget Constraint**: The total cost of procured materials must not exceed the budget.
    *   `4 * x[1,1] + 5 * x[1,2] + 6 * x[2,1] + 7 * x[2,2] <= 20`

3.  **Building Material Quality Standard Constraints**: The sum of quality ratings for each material type from selected suppliers, plus any quality shortfall `s[j]`, must meet or exceed the minimum quality standard for that material.
    *   For Material 1: `8 * x[1,1] + 7 * x[2,1] + s[1] >= 15`
    *   For Material 2: `9 * x[1,2] + 10 * x[2,2] + s[2] >= 18`

4.  **Variable Type Constraints**:
    *   `x[i,j]` are binary variables (0 or 1).
    *   `s[j]` are non-negative continuous variables (`s[j] >= 0`).

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Problem Background:
For chronic disease patients, formulating an effective long-term treatment pathway is crucial for improving quality of life, reducing acute attacks, and lowering medical costs. This optimization problem aims to design personalized, cost-effective treatment pathways for **two specific chronic disease patients**, Patient 1 and Patient 2, over **two distinct time periods**, Time Period 1 and Time Period 2.

Decision Variables:
*   **Treatment Pathway Intensity (x_it):** For each Patient `i` (where `i` can be Patient 1 or Patient 2) and each Time Period `t` (where `t` can be Time Period 1 or Time Period 2), we define a continuous decision variable `x_it`. This variable represents the "extent" or "intensity" of applying the designed treatment pathway for Patient `i` in Time Period `t`. The value of `x_it` can range from **0** (no application or zero intensity) to **1** (full application or maximum intensity).
*   **Resource Slack (s_k):** For each of the **two types of medical resources** (Resource 1 and Resource 2), we define a continuous slack variable `s_k`. This variable represents the amount of the respective resource `k` that remains unused. These slack variables must be **non-negative**.

Parameters:
*   **Treatment Pathway Costs (C_it and c_it):** The cost associated with applying the treatment pathway for Patient `i` in Time Period `t` is as follows:
    *   Patient 1, Time Period 1: **5 units**
    *   Patient 2, Time Period 1: **6 units**
    *   Patient 1, Time Period 2: **4 units**
    *   Patient 2, Time Period 2: **5 units**
*   **Health Outcome Improvement (H_it):** The health outcome improvement achieved by applying the treatment pathway for Patient `i` in Time Period `t` is:
    *   Patient 1, Time Period 1: **3 units**
    *   Patient 2, Time Period 1: **4 units**
    *   Patient 1, Time Period 2: **5 units**
    *   Patient 2, Time Period 2: **6 units**
*   **Weight for Health Outcome (λ):** The importance of maximizing health outcomes in the objective function is weighted by **λ = 1**.
*   **Penalty for Resource Slack (ρ):** A penalty of **ρ = 0.5** is incurred for each unit of unused resource, contributing to the total cost.
*   **Treatment Plan Compatibility Factors (c_ijt):** These parameters define specific interactions or considerations among treatment pathways. A value of **1** indicates a significant interaction for the combination of Patient `i` (as the reference), Patient `j` (as the interacting patient), and Time Period `t`. A value of **0** indicates no such interaction for the purpose of this constraint. The specific values are:
    *   `c_111 = 1`
    *   `c_221 = 1`
    *   `c_121 = 0`
    *   `c_122 = 0`
    *   `c_212 = 0`
    *   `c_222 = 1`
    *   `c_211 = 1`
    *   `c_112 = 0`
*   **Resource Usage per Unit of Treatment (r_kt):** The amount of medical resource `k` consumed per unit of treatment pathway intensity (`x_it`) in Time Period `t` is:
    *   Resource 1, Time Period 1: **1 unit**
    *   Resource 2, Time Period 1: **1 unit**
    *   Resource 1, Time Period 2: **1 unit**
    *   Resource 2, Time Period 2: **1 unit**
*   **Total Available Resources (R_k):** The maximum available quantity for each resource type is:
    *   Resource 1: **15 units**
    *   Resource 2: **15 units**
*   **Patient Budget (B_i):** The maximum allowable budget for each patient's treatment pathway across all time periods is:
    *   Patient 1: **25 units**
    *   Patient 2: **25 units**

Optimization Goals:
The primary goal is to **minimize** a combined objective value, which balances total treatment costs, health outcome improvements, and penalties for unused resources.
The objective function is formulated as:
Minimize: `(Total Cost of all applied treatment pathways) - (λ * Total Health Outcome Improvement from all applied treatment pathways) + (ρ * Total Penalty from unused resources)`

Substituting the numerical parameters and simplifying, the objective function is:
Minimize: `(5*x_11 + 6*x_21 + 4*x_12 + 5*x_22) - 1 * (3*x_11 + 4*x_21 + 5*x_12 + 6*x_22) + 0.5 * (s_1 + s_2)`
Which simplifies to:
Minimize: `2*x_11 + 2*x_21 - 1*x_12 - 1*x_22 + 0.5*s_1 + 0.5*s_2`

Problem Constraints:
1.  **Treatment Plan Compatibility Constraints:** These constraints ensure specific interactions between treatment pathways are managed.
    *   For Patient 1: `(1 * x_11 + 0 * x_21 + 0 * x_12 + 0 * x_22) <= 1` (This simplifies to `x_11 <= 1`, which is also covered by variable bounds).
    *   For Patient 2: `(1 * x_11 + 1 * x_21 + 0 * x_12 + 1 * x_22) <= 1` (This simplifies to `x_11 + x_21 + x_22 <= 1`).
2.  **Medical Resource Availability Constraints:** The total consumption of each medical resource by all applied treatment pathways (across both patients and both time periods) must not exceed the available amount. Any shortfall is covered by the slack variable.
    *   For Resource 1: `(1 * x_11 + 1 * x_21 + 1 * x_12 + 1 * x_22) + s_1 = 15`
    *   For Resource 2: `(1 * x_11 + 1 * x_21 + 1 * x_12 + 1 * x_22) + s_2 = 15`
3.  **Budget Constraints:** The total cost incurred by the treatment pathway for each patient, summed across both time periods, must not exceed that patient's allocated budget.
    *   For Patient 1: `(5 * x_11 + 4 * x_12) <= 25`
    *   For Patient 2: `(6 * x_21 + 5 * x_22) <= 25`
4.  **Decision Variable Bounds:**
    *   The intensity of each treatment pathway `x_it` must be between **0 and 1**.
    *   The slack variables `s_k` for unused resources must be **non-negative**.
