Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Agricultural Insurance Optimization Problem (Numerical Version)

Background
The agricultural insurance optimization problem involves how to reasonably design and price agricultural insurance products to reduce agricultural production risks, increase farmers' income, and achieve a balance between the profits and risk assumption of insurance companies. Effective agricultural insurance schemes can help farmers cope with uncontrollable factors such as natural disasters and climate change, ensuring the stability of food production.

This specific numerical instance considers two distinct agricultural insurance products, Product 1 and Product 2.

Decision Variables:
*   Let `x_i` be a binary variable, where `x_i = 1` if the farmer purchases agricultural insurance Product `i`, and `x_i = 0` otherwise.
*   Let `y_i` be a binary variable, where `y_i = 1` if the farmer receives compensation for agricultural insurance Product `i`, and `y_i = 0` otherwise.

Parameters:
*   For Product 1 (i=1):
    *   Maximum number of Product 1 a farmer can buy (`B_1`): 1
    *   Premium for Product 1 (`P_1`): 100 units
    *   Financial compensation amount received for Product 1 (`C_1`): 200 units
    *   Utility/Benefit for receiving compensation for Product 1 (`U_1`): 300 units
    *   Risk cost for buying Product 1 (`R_1`): 50 units
*   For Product 2 (i=2):
    *   Maximum number of Product 2 a farmer can buy (`B_2`): 1
    *   Premium for Product 2 (`P_2`): 150 units
    *   Financial compensation amount received for Product 2 (`C_2`): 250 units
    *   Utility/Benefit for receiving compensation for Product 2 (`U_2`): 400 units
    *   Risk cost for buying Product 2 (`R_2`): 60 units

Optimization Goals
The objective is to maximize the farmer's net utility, which is represented by the total benefit from receiving compensation minus the total risk cost associated with purchasing insurance products.
Maximize: `(300 * y_1 + 400 * y_2) - (50 * x_1 + 60 * x_2)`

Problem Constraints
The optimization must satisfy the following conditions:

1.  **Insurance purchase limit (Agricultural production risk constraints related to product availability):**
    Farmers can purchase at most one unit of each specific insurance product.
    *   `x_1 <= 1`
    *   `x_2 <= 1`

2.  **Insurance payout limitation (Insurance product type and limitation constraints):**
    Compensation for an insurance product can only be received if that product was actually purchased.
    *   `y_1 <= x_1`
    *   `y_2 <= x_2`

3.  **Farmers' economic status constraint:**
    The total premiums paid by the farmer must be greater than or equal to the total financial compensation received by the farmer. This implies that the farmer's net direct cash flow from the insurance products must be non-positive, focusing the benefit on the utility of risk reduction rather than direct cash profit from the transaction itself.
    *   `(100 * x_1 + 150 * x_2) - (200 * y_1 + 250 * y_2) >= 0`

All decision variables `x_1, x_2, y_1, y_2` are binary (0 or 1).

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization of Construction Plan in the Construction Industry
    Problem Background
    In the construction industry, the rational arrangement of construction plans is crucial for the successful completion of projects. This specific optimization problem aims to arrange two distinct construction tasks and allocate resources to them. The objective is to minimize the total construction cost, which is determined by the start times of these tasks. The arrangement must adhere to a logical dependency between the tasks and conform to basic resource availability limits.

    Optimization Goals
    - Minimize the total construction cost, which is directly influenced by the start times of the tasks.

    Decision Variables
    The problem involves two main types of decision variables:
    -   **t[0]**: A continuous variable representing the start time of Task 0.
    -   **t[1]**: A continuous variable representing the start time of Task 1.
    -   **x[0,0]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 0 utilizes Resource 0, and 0 otherwise.
    -   **x[0,1]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 1 utilizes Resource 0, and 0 otherwise.
    -   **x[1,0]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 0 utilizes Resource 1, and 0 otherwise.
    -   **x[1,1]**: A binary variable (0 or 1), where 1 indicates that Task 1 utilizes Resource 1, and 0 otherwise.

    Parameters
    The problem involves the following numerical parameters:
    -   **Number of Tasks**: There are 2 tasks in consideration, referred to as Task 0 and Task 1.
    -   **Number of Resources**: There are 2 resources in consideration, referred to as Resource 0 and Resource 1.
    -   **Task Durations**:
        -   Task 0 has a duration of 3 time units.
        -   Task 1 has a duration of 2 time units.
    -   **Task Unit Time Costs**:
        -   The unit time cost associated with Task 0 is 100 monetary units.
        -   The unit time cost associated with Task 1 is 150 monetary units.
    -   **Resource Availability Limits**:
        -   The availability limit for Resource 0 is 1 unit.
        -   The availability limit for Resource 1 is 1 unit.

    Objective Function
    The objective is to minimize the total construction cost, calculated as the sum of the unit time costs multiplied by their respective task start times:
    Minimize: `100 * t[0] + 150 * t[1]`

    Problem Constraints
    The construction plan must satisfy the following constraints:
    -   **Task Dependency Constraint**: Task 1 cannot commence until Task 0 has been fully completed. Given that Task 0 has a duration of 3 time units, this dependency is formulated as:
        `t[1] >= t[0] + 3`
    -   **Resource Availability Constraints**: The assignment of tasks to resources must respect the maximum availability of each resource. For each Resource `i` (where `i` can be 0 or 1) and each Task `j` (where `j` can be 0 or 1), the binary variable `x[i,j]` (indicating if Task `j` uses Resource `i`) must be less than or equal to the availability limit of Resource `i`. Specifically, these constraints are:
        -   `x[0,0] <= 1` (Task 0's utilization of Resource 0 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
        -   `x[0,1] <= 1` (Task 1's utilization of Resource 0 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
        -   `x[1,0] <= 1` (Task 0's utilization of Resource 1 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
        -   `x[1,1] <= 1` (Task 1's utilization of Resource 1 must not exceed its availability limit of 1).
    -   **Variable Type Constraints**:
        -   The decision variables `t[0]` and `t[1]` are continuous, meaning they can take any real value within their feasible range.
        -   The decision variables `x[0,0]`, `x[0,1]`, `x[1,0]`, and `x[1,1]` are binary, meaning they can only take values of 0 or 1.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
TechInnovate Online, a rapidly expanding e-commerce company specializing in consumer electronics, is facing challenges in efficiently managing the inventory of its popular product, the 'NextGen SmartWatch'. To optimize their operations and minimize costs, the company needs a precise inventory plan for the upcoming 8 weeks.

At the beginning of Week 1, TechInnovate Online has an existing inventory of 40 units of the NextGen SmartWatch in its main warehouse. The company incurs two primary costs associated with inventory management:

1.  **Ordering Cost:** For each unit of NextGen SmartWatch ordered from their supplier, there is an associated cost of $7. This covers administrative processing, handling, and initial inspection upon arrival.
2.  **Holding Cost:** Storing each unit of the NextGen SmartWatch in the warehouse costs $3 per unit per week. This includes warehousing space, insurance, and potential obsolescence.

The marketing department has provided the following deterministic demand forecast for the NextGen SmartWatch over the next 8 weeks:

| Week | Forecasted Demand (Units) |
|------|---------------------------|
| 1    | 90                        |
| 2    | 110                       |
| 3    | 130                       |
| 4    | 100                       |
| 5    | 120                       |
| 6    | 140                       |
| 7    | 95                        |
| 8    | 125                       |

TechInnovate Online aims to develop an inventory strategy that satisfies all customer demand promptly while minimizing the total inventory-related costs (ordering and holding) over this 8-week planning horizon. All units ordered in a given week are assumed to be available to meet the demand within that same week. Additionally, the company cannot allow for any stockouts, meaning all demand must be met from available inventory, and inventory levels at the end of each week must be non-negative.

Your task is to determine the optimal quantity of NextGen SmartWatches to order in each of the 8 weeks and the resulting inventory level at the end of each week, such that the total ordering and holding costs are minimized over the entire planning period, subject to meeting all customer demand.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Green Valley Farms, a large agricultural enterprise, is preparing for the upcoming planting season. The farm spans 500 acres of fertile land. The management needs to make a critical decision: which single type of crop to plant for the entire 500 acres to maximize profitability for the season. The primary concern is the uncertainty surrounding future market prices and overall yield conditions, which are highly dependent on broader economic factors and regional weather patterns.

After careful analysis of historical data and market forecasts, Green Valley Farms has identified three potential crop choices and three distinct market/yield conditions, each with an estimated probability of occurring. The net profit per acre for each crop under each market/yield condition has been estimated as follows:

**Crop Options:**
1.  **Corn**
2.  **Soybeans**
3.  **Winter Wheat**

**Market/Yield Conditions and Their Probabilities:**
*   **Condition S1: Favorable Market & Good Yield** (e.g., high demand, ideal weather): Probability 0.35
*   **Condition S2: Moderate Market & Normal Yield** (e.g., stable demand, average weather): Probability 0.45
*   **Condition S3: Unfavorable Market & Poor Yield** (e.g., low demand, adverse weather): Probability 0.20

**Estimated Net Profit per Acre (in USD) for Each Crop Under Each Condition:**

| Crop          | Condition S1 (Favorable Market & Good Yield) | Condition S2 (Moderate Market & Normal Yield) | Condition S3 (Unfavorable Market & Poor Yield) |
|---------------|----------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------|

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Charging Station Construction (Numerical Version)

**Problem Background**
The optimization problem of charging station construction involves how to reasonably allocate the location and number of charging stations in a region to meet the charging needs of electric vehicle users. This problem has practical application value in promoting the popularization of electric vehicles, improving the utilization rate of charging facilities, and reducing dependence on energy resources.

This specific numerical instance considers a region with 2 potential locations for charging station construction, indexed as 0 and 1.

**Decision Variables**
For each potential location `i` in the set `{0, 1}`, a binary decision variable `x[i]` is defined:
*   `x[i] = 1` if a charging station is built at location `i`.
*   `x[i] = 0` if a charging station is not built at location `i`.

**Parameters**
*   **User Demand (`a`):** The minimum number of charging stations required to meet the quantity needs of electric vehicle users in the region is `1`.
*   **Capacity Demand (`b`):** The minimum number of charging stations required to meet the overall charging station capacity needs in the region is `2`.
*   **Construction Costs (`c_construction`):**
    *   Construction cost for a charging station at location 0 is `3` units.
    *   Construction cost for a charging station at location 1 is `4` units.
*   **Operation Cost (`c_operation`):** The operating cost for any single charging station (if built) is `1` unit.

**Optimization Goals**
Minimize the total cost, which is composed of the construction costs and the operating costs for all built charging stations.
*   The objective function is defined as:
    Minimize `(3 * x[0] + 1) + (4 * x[1] + 1)`
    Which simplifies to:
    Minimize `3 * x[0] + 4 * x[1] + 2`

*   The goals of maximizing charging convenience for electric vehicle users and improving the utilization rate of charging stations and reducing user waiting time are addressed implicitly by the demand and capacity constraints, but are not explicitly quantified in the objective function with specific numerical terms in this formulation.

**Problem Constraints**
The optimization problem is subject to the following numerical constraints:

1.  **Electric Vehicle User Number Constraint:**
    The total number of charging stations built must be greater than or equal to the minimum requirement for electric vehicle users.
    `x[0] + x[1] >= 1`

2.  **Charging Station Capacity Constraint:**
    The total number of charging stations built must be greater than or equal to the minimum required capacity.
    `x[0] + x[1] >= 2`

*   The "Charging station location constraint" is implicitly handled by the definition of the available locations {0, 1} and the binary decision variables `x[i]`.
*   The "Charging equipment performance constraint" is assumed to be met by any station built and is not explicitly formulated with numerical values in the provided code.

The goal is to determine the binary values for `x[0]` and `x[1]` that minimize the total cost while satisfying all specified constraints.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
The Guardian Frontier Agency (GFA) is responsible for securing a challenging and dynamic segment of the national border. To enhance their operational capabilities, the agency has been allocated a special annual budget of $5,000,000 specifically for acquiring and deploying new surveillance and interdiction assets. The GFA aims to allocate this budget among various asset types to maximize the overall effectiveness of their border security operations.

The agency has identified five key asset categories, each contributing differently to the 'Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score' per million dollars allocated. This score represents a comprehensive measure of an asset's ability to deter, detect, and respond to illegal border activities.

Here are the details for each asset category:

*   **High-Altitude Surveillance Drones (HSD)**: These drones provide wide-area aerial reconnaissance and early warning capabilities. For every $1,000,000 allocated to HSD, the expected Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score increases by 8.5 points.
*   **Ground-Based Sensor Networks (GSN)**: These systems offer continuous, covert monitoring along critical pathways and remote areas. For every $1,000,000 allocated to GSN, the expected Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score increases by 7.0 points.
*   **All-Terrain Patrol Vehicles (ATV)**: These vehicles enable rapid response and ground interdiction capabilities. For every $1,000,000 allocated to ATV, the expected Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score increases by 6.0 points.
*   **Specialized K9 Detection Teams (K9T)**: Highly effective for detecting concealed contraband and individuals, these teams combine human and canine capabilities. For every $1,000,000 allocated to K9T, the expected Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score increases by 9.0 points.
*   **Advanced Night Vision Equipment (NVE)**: This equipment enhances the effectiveness of existing human patrols during low-light conditions. For every $1,000,000 allocated to NVE, the expected Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score increases by 7.5 points.

To ensure a balanced and effective security strategy, the GFA has established the following operational and budgetary guidelines:

1.  The entire special annual budget of $5,000,000 must be utilized for these new asset allocations.
2.  To ensure a baseline of continuous, covert monitoring, at least 15% of the total budget must be allocated to Ground-Based Sensor Networks.
3.  Due to the complexities of drone operations, maintenance, and airspace regulations, the allocation for High-Altitude Surveillance Drones cannot exceed 30% of the total budget.
4.  To maintain robust active response and interdiction capabilities, the combined allocation for All-Terrain Patrol Vehicles and Specialized K9 Detection Teams must be at least 45% of the total budget.
5.  Advanced Night Vision Equipment is considered a supplementary asset; therefore, its allocation should not exceed 10% of the total budget.
6.  No asset category can receive a negative budget allocation.

The GFA needs to determine the optimal proportion of the $5,000,000 budget to allocate to each of the five asset categories to maximize the total Integrated Threat Interception Efficacy Score. Your task is to formulate this problem to advise the GFA on their resource allocation strategy.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Agricultural Waste Disposal

Problem Background
The optimization of agricultural waste disposal involves how to effectively deal with the waste generated in agricultural production. There are two types of agricultural waste, referred to as Waste Type 1 and Waste Type 2, which need to be processed at two available disposal facilities, Facility 1 and Facility 2. A reasonable waste disposal scheme aims to reduce environmental pollution, improve resource utilization efficiency, and minimize the cost of waste disposal.

Optimization Objectives
The objective is to minimize the total cost, which includes the cost of processing waste at facilities, a penalty cost associated with the environmental impact of emissions, and a cost for any waste that is not processed.
Specifically, the objective function is to minimize:
`(5 + 1) * x[1,1] + (6 + 2) * x[1,2] + (7 + 3) * x[2,1] + (8 + 4) * x[2,2] + 10 * w[1] + 12 * w[2]`
where:
- `x[i,j]` represents the quantity of Waste Type `i` processed at Facility `j`.
- `w[i]` represents the quantity of Waste Type `i` that is not processed.
- The values `5, 6, 7, 8` are the unit processing costs for `x[1,1], x[1,2], x[2,1], x[2,2]` respectively.
- The values `1, 2, 3, 4` are the emission factors per unit of waste processed for `x[1,1], x[1,2], x[2,1], x[2,2]` respectively, treated as a cost in the objective function.
- The values `10` and `12` are the costs per unit for not processing Waste Type 1 and Waste Type 2, respectively.

Problem Constraints
The waste disposal scheme must adhere to the following constraints:

1.  **Waste Generation Constraints (Waste Balance):** The total quantity of each waste type processed at all facilities plus the quantity of that waste type left unprocessed must equal the total generated quantity of that waste type.
    *   For Waste Type 1: `x[1,1] + x[1,2] + w[1] == 10` (where `10` is the generated quantity of Waste Type 1).
    *   For Waste Type 2: `x[2,1] + x[2,2] + w[2] == 20` (where `20` is the generated quantity of Waste Type 2).

2.  **Disposal Facility Capacity Constraints:** The total quantity of waste processed at each facility cannot exceed its specific processing capacity.
    *   For Facility 1: `x[1,1] + x[2,1] <= 15` (where `15` is the processing capacity of Facility 1).
    *   For Facility 2: `x[1,2] + x[2,2] <= 25` (where `25` is the processing capacity of Facility 2).

3.  **Environmental Emission Standard Constraints:** The total environmental emissions generated from all waste processing activities must not exceed a specified maximum acceptable level.
    *   Total Emissions: `(1 * x[1,1]) + (2 * x[1,2]) + (3 * x[2,1]) + (4 * x[2,2]) <= 50` (where `50` is the maximum acceptable total emissions).
    *   The values `1, 2, 3, 4` are the emission factors per unit of waste processed for `x[1,1], x[1,2], x[2,1], x[2,2]` respectively.

4.  **Non-negativity Constraints:** All decision variables `x[i,j]` and `w[i]` must be non-negative continuous values.

    *   **Cost per staff member**: $1,900 for the academic year.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Optimization Problem of Agricultural Veterinary Scheduling and Planning

    Problem Background
    The optimization of agricultural veterinary scheduling and planning involves how to effectively arrange the work schedule of veterinarians to meet the health needs of farm animals. There are **2** farms (Farm 0 and Farm 1) and a limited number of veterinarians. Specifically, there are **2** veterinarians (Veterinarian 0 and Veterinarian 1) available for scheduling. The planning horizon is divided into **2** discrete time slots (Time Slot 0 and Time Slot 1). The goal is to reasonably schedule the time and resources of these **2** veterinarians to ensure animal health and improve the efficiency of veterinary services for the **2** farms over the **2** time slots.

    Optimization Goals
    The primary goal is to maximize the total net benefit derived from veterinarian visits. This net benefit is calculated by considering the health benefits gained from visits and the costs incurred.
    - Maximize the health status of farm animals: Each visit by any veterinarian to any farm at any time slot contributes a uniform health benefit of **10** units.
    - Optimize the scheduling plan of veterinarians to improve work efficiency: This is implicitly addressed by maximizing the net benefit.
    - Minimize the route of veterinary rounds to reduce costs: Each visit by any veterinarian to any farm incurs a uniform patrol cost of **5** units.
    The combined objective is to maximize the sum of `(10 * x[i, j, t] - 5 * D[j] * x[i, j, t])` for all veterinarians `i` in `{0, 1}`, farms `j` in `{0, 1}`, and time slots `t` in `{0, 1}`. Given that the health demand parameter `D[j]` is **1** for both farms, this objective simplifies to maximizing `(10 - 5) * x[i, j, t] = 5 * x[i, j, t]` for each visit, meaning the total objective is to maximize the sum of **5** for every visit made.

    Problem Constraints
    - Veterinarian number constraint: At any given farm (Farm 0 or Farm 1) and any given time slot (Time Slot 0 or Time Slot 1), the maximum number of veterinarians that can be present simultaneously is **2**.
    - Animal health needs constraint: Animals on each farm have specific health needs. Farm 0 requires a total of at least **1** visit (from any veterinarian across all time slots), and Farm 1 also requires a total of at least **1** visit (from any veterinarian across all time slots).
    - Rounds time window constraint: Each veterinarian (Veterinarian 0 or Veterinarian 1) in each time slot (Time Slot 0 or Time Slot 1) must be assigned to visit exactly one farm (Farm 0 or Farm 1). This ensures that a veterinarian is uniquely occupied at a specific farm during each time slot and cannot be in multiple places at once.

To ensure network reliability, a field technician is assigned to perform routine checks and minor maintenance at several key network nodes daily. For today's shift, the technician needs to visit six specific network nodes. The estimated travel times (in minutes) between the central depot and these nodes, as well as between each pair of nodes, are provided in the table below. These times account for typical traffic conditions during operational hours.

**Locations to Visit:**
*   Central Depot (D)
*   Network Node A (NA)
*   Network Node B (NB)
*   Network Node C (NC)
*   Network Node D (ND)
*   Network Node E (NE)
*   Network Node F (NF)

| From / To | D  | NA | NB | NC | ND | NE | NF |
| :-------- | :- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- |

| ND        | 25 | 10 | 22 | 15 | -  | 16 | 11 |
| NE        | 18 | 14 | 8  | 20 | 16 | -  | 13 |
| NF        | 22 | 20 | 15 | 12 | 11 | 13 | -  |


**Your Task:**
Determine the optimal sequence of visits for the technician to minimize the total travel time for their complete tour. The tour must start at the Central Depot, visit each of the six network nodes exactly once, and end back at the Central Depot.

**Objective:** Minimize the total travel time for the technician's route.

**Requirements:**
1.  Identify the complete tour, listing the sequence of locations visited (e.g., D -> NA -> NB -> ... -> D).
2.  Calculate the total travel time for this determined tour.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
A leading Big Data Analytics company is re-evaluating its data distribution network to optimize service delivery and operational costs. The company operates two primary data centers and is considering establishing regional data hubs to efficiently serve its client zones. The goal is to design an optimal network configuration that minimizes total costs while meeting client demands and respecting operational capacities.

**Primary Data Centers:**
The company has two primary data centers with the following processing and outgoing data capacities:
*   Data Center A: Maximum outgoing data capacity of 500 Terabytes (TB) per day.
*   Data Center B: Maximum outgoing data capacity of 300 Terabytes (TB) per day.

**Potential Regional Data Hub Locations:**
There are three potential locations for establishing regional data hubs. Each hub incurs a fixed setup cost if opened, and has a maximum data throughput capacity:
*   Regional Data Hub 1: Setup cost $50,000, maximum daily throughput capacity of 400 TB.
*   Regional Data Hub 2: Setup cost $40,000, maximum daily throughput capacity of 350 TB.
*   Regional Data Hub 3: Setup cost $45,000, maximum daily throughput capacity of 300 TB.

**Client Zones and Daily Data Demands:**
The company serves four distinct client zones, each with a daily data demand:
*   Client Zone 1: Requires 200 TB of processed data per day.
*   Client Zone 2: Requires 250 TB of processed data per day.
*   Client Zone 3: Requires 150 TB of processed data per day.
*   Client Zone 4: Requires 200 TB of processed data per day.

**Data Transfer Costs (per Terabyte):**
The costs associated with transferring one Terabyte of data between facilities are as follows:

*   **From Primary Data Centers to Regional Data Hubs:**
    *   Data Center A to Hub 1: $2
    *   Data Center A to Hub 2: $3
    *   Data Center A to Hub 3: $4
    *   Data Center B to Hub 1: $3
    *   Data Center B to Hub 2: $2
    *   Data Center B to Hub 3: $3

*   **From Regional Data Hubs to Client Zones:**
    *   Hub 1 to Zone 1: $3
    *   Hub 1 to Zone 2: $4
    *   Hub 1 to Zone 3: $5
    *   Hub 1 to Zone 4: $4
    *   Hub 2 to Zone 1: $4
    *   Hub 2 to Zone 2: $3
    *   Hub 2 to Zone 3: $4
    *   Hub 2 to Zone 4: $5
    *   Hub 3 to Zone 1: $5
    *   Hub 3 to Zone 2: $4
    *   Hub 3 to Zone 3: $3
    *   Hub 3 to Zone 4: $4

**Operational Requirements and Constraints:**
*   Regional data hubs act purely as transfer points; they do not store data. This means that for any activated hub, the total daily incoming data must precisely equal its total daily outgoing data.
*   All data demands from the client zones must be met completely.
*   The total daily data output from each primary data center cannot exceed its specified capacity.
*   If a regional data hub is activated (opened), the total daily data throughput (flow through it, either incoming or outgoing) cannot exceed its maximum capacity.

**Your Task:**
Based on the information provided, determine the most cost-effective data distribution network configuration for the company.
1.  Identify which regional data hubs the company should activate (open).
2.  Detail the optimal daily data transfer plan, specifying the quantity of data (in TB) to be transferred on each route from primary data centers, through the activated regional hubs, to each client zone.
3.  Calculate the minimum total daily cost, which includes the fixed setup costs for all activated regional data hubs and the variable data transfer costs.

The primary goal is to enhance security, minimize inmate movement risks, and improve staff efficiency by carefully positioning departments relative to each other. A higher value indicates a more critical need for proximity to minimize security risks, staff time, or operational friction during necessary interactions.\n\n| From/To | H_max | H_med | DH | MU | VA | GCC |\n|---------|-------|-------|----|----|----|-----|\n| H_max   | -     | 20    | 60 | 50 | 80 | 70  |\n| H_med   | 20    | -     | 40 | 30 | 55 | 45  |\n| DH      | 60    | 40    | -  | 15 | 5  | 20  |\

| VA      | 80    | 55    | 5  | 5  | -  | 30  |\
| GCC     | 70    | 45    | 20 | 25 | 30 | -   |\n\n**Distances Between Locations:**\nThe physical distances (in meters) between the centroids of the available locations are provided in the following matrix. These distances represent the path inmates and staff would travel between any two locations.\n\n| From/To | L1 | L2 | L3 | L4 | L5 | L6 |\n|---------|----|----|----|----|----|----|\n| L1      | -  | 10 | 20 | 15 | 25 | 35 |\n| L2      | 10 | -  | 10 | 25 | 15 | 25 |\
| L3      | 20 | 10 | -  | 35 | 25 | 15 |\
| L4      | 15 | 25 | 35 | -  | 10 | 20 |\
| L5      | 25 | 15 | 25 | 10 | -  | 10 |\
| L6      | 35 | 25 | 15 | 20 | 10 | -  |\n\n**Task:**\nDetermine the optimal assignment of each operational unit to one of the available locations. Each unit must be assigned to exactly one location, and each location can only house one unit.\n\n**Optimization Goal:**\nThe primary objective is to minimize the total sum of the 'interaction cost' multiplied by the 'distance' for all pairs of operational units. This total sum represents the overall operational inefficiency and security risk across the entire facility.

1.  The total quantity of circuit boards shipped from each plant cannot exceed its weekly production capacity.

Solve the following mathmetical modeling problem
Park Site Selection Planning Optimization Problem
Problem Background
Park site selection planning involves finding the best location in the city to build a park. For this problem, there are **two potential park locations**, designated as Location 1 and Location 2. The goal is to provide leisure and entertainment venues, improve the quality of life for residents, and meet the requirements of urban greening and planning. This problem requires a comprehensive consideration of factors such as land use, resident needs, and transportation convenience to achieve scientific and reasonable planning for park site selection.

Optimization Goals
The objective is to **maximize** a combined score that reflects the benefits and costs. Specifically:
- **Maximize the service range of the park, benefiting more residents:** Each unit of service range provided by a park at Location 1 contributes **10 units** to the objective, and each unit of service range from Location 2 contributes **15 units**.
- **Optimize park site selection, improving the level of urban greening:** This is achieved by deciding which locations to build parks.
- **Consider factors such as land cost and transportation convenience to ensure the feasibility of the site selection:** Building a park at Location 1 incurs a cost of **5 units**, and building a park at Location 2 incurs a cost of **8 units**. Additionally, there is a penalty for any unmet resident demand, with each unit of unmet demand reducing the objective by **2 units**.

Problem Constraints
- **Land use planning constraints:** The decision to build a park at a given location is a binary choice (either build or not build).
- **Resident needs constraints:** The total service range provided by all selected parks, combined with any unmet demand, must be at least the total resident demand. The resident demand for the area served by Location 1 is **30 units**, and for Location 2 is **40 units**. Therefore, the total service provided plus unmet demand must be at least **70 units**.
- **Transportation convenience constraints:** For each potential location, a traffic accessibility factor is considered. For Location 1, this factor is **0.5**, and for Location 2, it is **0.7**. If a park is selected at a location, its traffic accessibility factor multiplied by the selection decision must be non-negative.
- **Service range linking constraints:** The service range provided by a park at a specific location can only be non-zero if a park is actually built at that location. If a park is not built at a location, its service range must be zero. If a park is built, its service range can be up to a large number (e.g., **100** units).
- All service range values and unmet demand must be non-negative.

- **Transportation convenience constraints:** For each potential location, a traffic accessibility factor is considered. For Location 1, this factor is **0.5**, and for Location 2, it is **0.7**. If a park is selected at a location, its traffic accessibility factor multiplied by the selection decision must be non-negative.
- **Service range linking constraints:** The service range provided by a park at a specific location can only be non-zero if a park is actually built at that location. If a park is not built at a location, its service range must be zero. If a park is built, its service range can be up to a large number (e.g., **100** units).
- All service range values and unmet demand must be non-negative.

## Scientific Research Initiative: Optimizing Task Allocation and Scheduling

A leading biomedical research institute is launching a critical new initiative focused on developing novel diagnostics for a prevalent disease. This initiative involves a series of interconnected research tasks that must be completed efficiently by a multidisciplinary team within a tight 5-day work week, starting on Monday and concluding on Friday. The project lead aims to optimize the assignment of these tasks to the available researchers to minimize the overall effort expenditure while respecting individual expertise, workload limits, and daily operational constraints.

### Research Team Members and Capacities:
The research team consists of four key members, each with varying expertise and weekly task capacities:

1.  **Dr. Anya Sharma (Senior Researcher):** Highly experienced in experimental design and data interpretation. Can oversee a maximum of **4 tasks** during the 5-day week.
2.  **Dr. Ben Carter (Post-doctoral Fellow):** Skilled across various lab techniques and data analysis. Can undertake a maximum of **5 tasks** during the 5-day week.
3.  **Carly Davis (PhD Student):** Proficient in lab procedures and basic bioinformatics. Can undertake a maximum of **5 tasks** during the 5-day week.
4.  **David Evans (Lab Technician):** Specialized in core laboratory techniques. Can undertake a maximum of **5 tasks** during the 5-day week.

### Research Tasks and Skill Requirements:
The initiative requires the completion of 8 distinct tasks. Each task has specific skill requirements:

*   **Task T1: Comprehensive Literature Review and Hypothesis Refinement:** Requires strong analytical and scientific writing skills.
*   **Task T2: Detailed Experimental Protocol Design:** Requires advanced experimental design knowledge and domain expertise.
*   **Task T3: Cell Culture Maintenance and Sample Preparation:** Requires precise aseptic technique and laboratory skills.
*   **Task T4: PCR and Gel Electrophoresis Procedures:** Requires proficiency in molecular biology lab techniques.
*   **Task T5: Advanced Microscopy Imaging and Preliminary Analysis:** Requires expertise in operating microscopes and basic image processing.
*   **Task T6: Bioinformatics Raw Data Preprocessing:** Requires proficiency in scripting (e.g., Python/R) and command-line tools for data handling.
*   **Task T7: Statistical Analysis of Experimental Results:** Requires strong statistical background and data interpretation skills.
*   **Task T8: Drafting Initial Research Report Section:** Requires scientific writing and synthesis skills.

### Effort Units per Task-Staff Assignment:
The table below shows the estimated "effort units" required for each researcher to successfully complete each task. A lower number of effort units indicates greater efficiency or less resources consumed for that assignment. A dash (-) in the table indicates that a researcher does not possess the necessary skills for that specific task and therefore cannot be assigned to it.

| Task \ Researcher    | Dr. Anya Sharma | Dr. Ben Carter | Carly Davis | David Evans |
|:---------------------|:----------------|:---------------|:------------|:------------|
| T1: Lit Review       | 10              | 12             | 15          | -           |
| T2: Exp Protocol     | 12              | 14             | -           | -           |
| T3: Cell Culture     | -               | -              | 10          | 8           |
| T4: PCR/Gel          | -               | 15             | 12          | 10          |
| T5: Microscopy       | 15              | 16             | -           | 14          |
| T6: Bioinfo Preproc  | -               | -              | 12          | -           |
| T7: Stats Analysis   | 13              | 15             | -           | -           |
| T8: Report Draft     | 14              | 16             | 18          | -           |

### Optimization Goal and Constraints:
The institute's project lead needs to determine the optimal assignment of tasks to researchers over the 5-day work week (Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday, Friday). Your task is to construct an operations research model to achieve the following:

**Objective:**
*   Minimize the *total sum of effort units* expended across all completed tasks for the entire initiative.

**Constraints:**
*   **Task Completion:** Each of the 8 distinct research tasks must be fully completed exactly once during the 5-day planning period.
*   **Skill Matching:** A researcher can only be assigned a task for which they possess the required skills (as indicated by a numerical effort unit in the table above).
*   **Weekly Workload Limits:** Each researcher must not exceed their specified maximum number of tasks for the entire 5-day week.
*   **Daily Workload Limit:** No researcher can be assigned more than one task on any given day.

Your model should determine which researcher is assigned to each task, and on which specific day, to meet these requirements.

An elderly care facility, 'Sunshine Haven,' is committed to providing healthy, balanced, and cost-effective meals for its residents. The facility's dietitian is tasked with creating a daily meal plan for a representative resident, aiming to satisfy all essential nutritional requirements while minimizing the total daily food cost.

The dietitian has selected five staple food items that are regularly available. Each item is provided in a standard serving size with known nutritional content and cost, as detailed below:

**Food Items and Nutritional Information (per serving):**

| Food Item           | Cost per Serving ($) | Calories (kcal) | Protein (g) | Vitamin C (mg) | Calcium (mg) | Iron (mg) |
| :------------------ | :------------------- | :-------------- | :---------- | :------------- | :----------- | :-------- |

| Skim Milk           | 0.30                 | 70              | 7           | 2              | 250          | 0.1       |
| Boiled Egg          | 0.40                 | 78              | 6           | 0              | 30           | 1         |
| Cooked Chicken Breast | 2.00                 | 165             | 31          | 0              | 10           | 1.5       |
| Orange              | 0.75                 | 62              | 1           | 70             | 55           | 0.1       |

To maintain the residents' health and well-being, the daily meal plan for each resident must strictly adhere to the following nutritional guidelines:

*   **Calories**: The total caloric intake must be a minimum of 1800 kcal and must not exceed 2200 kcal.
*   **Protein**: The diet must provide at least 50g of protein.
*   **Vitamin C**: A minimum of 60mg of Vitamin C must be included.
*   **Calcium**: The daily calcium intake must be a minimum of 1000mg and a maximum of 1500mg.
*   **Iron**: At least 10mg of iron is required.

**Problem Requirements:**

1.  Formulate a complete linear programming model that accurately describes this diet planning problem.
2.  Using an appropriate solver, determine the optimal number of servings for each food item to be included in the daily diet.
3.  Calculate the minimum total daily cost per resident based on the optimal diet plan.
